Fifth Proof: Distinct Concepts of Knowing and Powerful
Fifth proof uses distinct concepts to show attributes not identical to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the distinctness of the concepts of knowing and powerful shows that the attributes are not identical to the divine essence.

Core Idea
Different concepts cannot be the same thing as the essence.

The fifth proof from al-Matalib al-Aliyah builds on a simple observation: we can think of a powerful being that is not knowing, and a knowing being that is not powerful. This shows that the concepts of 'powerful' and 'knowing' are different. If each were identical to God's essence, then the essence would have to be two different things at once – an impossibility. Let's see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Pay attention to the key terms: مفهوم (concept), ماهية (quiddity), حد (definition).
The translation is literal; the commentary will clarify the reasoning.
2
Identify the two premises
The passage gives two main premises: (1) The concept of powerful is different from the concept of knowing (because one can exist without the other). (2) Therefore their quiddities and definitions are different.
A 'quiddity' is the essence or nature of something.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
If each attribute (knowing, powerful) were identical to the essence, then the one essence would simultaneously be both – making it two different things, which is impossible. Therefore, the attributes are distinct from the essence.
The argument does not deny God is both knowing and powerful; it only denies that the concepts are identical to the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : إن المفهوم من كون الذات قادرة ، غير المفهوم من كونها عالمة . وذلك لأن القادر قد يكون عالماً ، وقد لا يكون ، كما أن العالم قد يكون قادراً وقد لا يكون . فلما كان ماهية العالمية غير ماهية القادرية ، وحد العالمية غير حد القادرية ، فلو قلنا : إنها عين الذات لزم أن يكون الشيء الواحد : لا يكون شيئاً واحداً . بل يكون شيئين متغايرين . وذلك محال .
The fifth proof: The concept of the essence being powerful is different from the concept of it being knowing. That is because the powerful may be knowing or may not be, just as the knowing may be powerful or may not be. So since the quiddity of being-knowing is different from the quiddity of being-powerful, and the definition of being-knowing is different from the definition of being-powerful, if we said that each is identical to the essence, then the one thing would not be one thing, but would be two different things, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
In this fifth proof, the author argues from the distinctness of the concepts (mafhum) of 'knowing' and 'powerful'. A powerful being may or may not be knowing, and a knowing being may or may not be powerful. Their quiddities (mahiyyat) and definitions (hudud) are different. If each attribute were identical to the essence, then the essence would be simultaneously two different things, which is absurd. Thus, the attributes must be distinct from the essence.

Key Terms
مفهوم
ماهية
حد
عالمية
قادرية
تغاير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this proof denies that God is both knowing and powerful, or that it contradicts His perfection.
Correction: The proof only denies that the concepts (mafhum) of knowing and powerful are identical to the essence. God is indeed both knowing and powerful, but His attributes are distinct realities added to His essence.

Checkpoint
What logical problem arises if 'knowing' and 'powerful' are both identical to the essence?
A) The essence would be eternal and temporal at once.
B) The essence would be both knowing and not knowing.
C) The essence would have to be two different things simultaneously, which is impossible.
D) The essence would be contingent.

Key Takeaway
The distinctness of the concepts of knowing and powerful proves that they cannot be identical to the divine essence; otherwise the essence would be two different things, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that God is both knowing and powerful, but have you ever truly reflected on the fact that these are distinct concepts? How does your understanding of God change when you realize that knowing and powerful are not the same thing? What does this teach you about the majesty of His attributes? Will you pause to ponder this distinction in your prayers today?
?

?

What does this say about the effort required to know God? Will you commit to learning more about each attribute individually?

Sixth Proof: Known Objects Are Not All Possible
Sixth proof uses the fact that some known objects are not possible to show knowledge and power differ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scope of God's knowledge and power differ, and why the impossibility of the necessary and impossible being objects of power but not knowledge demonstrates that knowledge and power are distinct attributes.

Core Idea
God knows even the impossible, but His power extends only to the possible.

This proof uses a simple logical argument to distinguish between two divine attributes. By examining what God knows versus what He has power over, we see that the necessary and impossible are known but not possible, which shows that knowledge and power are not the same. This lesson walks through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothesis
Start by grasping the conditional hypothesis: what would follow if knowledge and power were identical?
2
Examine the implication
If the hypothesis were true, then everything known would be within God's power.
3
Observe the counterexample
Notice that the necessary-of-existence and impossible-of-existence are known to God but are not within His power.
The necessary necessarily exists, the impossible cannot exist.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the counterexample contradicts the implication, the hypothesis is false, and knowledge and power are distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : لو كان كونه عالماً ، عين كونه قادراً ، لكان كل ما صح كونه عالماً به وجب أن يصح كونه قادراً عليه ، فكان يلزم في الواجب لذاته ، وفي الممتنع لذاته أن يكون مقدوراً ، كما أنه معلوم له وحيث أطبق أهل العقل أن الواجب لذاته والممتنع لذاته معلوم ، ( وليس بمقدور علمنا أن المفهوم من كون الشيء معلوماً ، مغاير للمفهوم من كونه مقدوراً ) (٢) وذلك يقتضي حصول المغايرة بين العلم وبين القدرة .
The sixth proof: If His being knowing were identical to His being powerful, then everything that is correct for Him to know would necessarily be correct for Him to have power over, and then it would follow that the necessary-of-existence-in-itself and the impossible-of-existence-in-itself would be possible, just as they are known to Him. And since the people of intellect agree that the necessary-in-itself and the impossible-in-itself are known (and not possible), we know that the concept of a thing being known is different from the concept of it being possible. That necessitates the existence of difference between knowledge and power.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
The sixth proof argues from the scope of knowledge versus power. God knows everything, including the necessary (wajib) and the impossible (mumtani'), but He does not have power (qudra) over the impossible (since it is inherently impossible). If knowledge and power were identical, then whatever is known would also be within His power, which is false. Therefore, the concepts are distinct, and the attributes themselves must be distinct from the essence.

Key Terms
معلوم
مقدور
واجب لذاته
ممتنع لذاته
مغايرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God knows something, He must have power over it.
Correction: The proof shows that God knows the necessary and impossible, but He does not have power over them, so knowledge and power are distinct. This does not limit God's power; it affirms that impossibility is not an object of power.

Checkpoint
What does the sixth proof use to show that knowledge and power are distinct?
A) God knows everything but does not have power over the impossible.
B) God's power is limited to possible things.
C) Knowledge and power are both eternal.
D) The necessary being is known but not possible.

Key Takeaway
The scope of God's knowledge is broader than His power: He knows the necessary and impossible, but His power only extends to the possible, proving knowledge and power are distinct attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever asked God to change something that, by His own nature, is impossible? How does this lesson reshape your understanding of what is appropriate to pray for?
?
If you truly believe that God's knowledge of your failures does not mean He will necessarily power them into existence, how does that change your responsibility to avoid sin?
?
When you face a situation that seems impossible to change, do you nonetheless trust that God knows it fully, while accepting that He may not—by His wisdom—make it possible? Where in your life do you need to surrender the impossible to God's knowledge and trust His power in the possible?

Seventh Proof: Knowledge Persists After Power Ceases
Seventh proof shows that after a possible object exists, power ceases but knowledge persists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the seventh proof demonstrates that knowledge and power are distinct divine attributes by showing that after a possible object exists, power ceases while knowledge remains.

Core Idea
After existence, an object is known forever, but can no longer be powered.

The seventh proof is a short but powerful argument. It focuses on what happens to a possible object once it comes into existence. The author shows that the object remains known but is no longer within God's power (since bringing it into existence again is impossible). This simple observation requires that knowledge and power be different attributes of God. Read the proof carefully to follow the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms like 'tahsil al-hasil' (attaining what is already attained).
2
Identify the key premise
The proof relies on the principle that bringing into existence something already existing is impossible (tahsil al-hasil). This makes the object no longer an object of power.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the object remains known after ceasing to be possible, knowledge and power must be distinct attributes.
This conclusion is stated directly: 'the truth of this negation and affirmation necessitates the difference between knowledge and power.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : إن القادر إذا خرج مقدوره إلى الوجود . لم يبق قادراً على إيجاده بعينه. لأن إيجاد الموجد وتحصيل الحاصل محال . والمحال لا قدرة عليه ، فالمقدور بعد دخوله في الوجود لم يبق مقدوراً ، لكنه بقي معلوماً بعد خروجه إلى الوجود. وصدق هذا النفي ، والإثبات ، يوجب التغاير بين العلم. وبين القدرة
The seventh proof: If the powerful one brings his possible object into existence, he is no longer powerful over bringing it into existence again, because bringing what exists into existence and attaining what is attained are impossible. And what is impossible cannot be an object of power. So the possible object, after entering into existence, is no longer a possible object, but it remains known after its coming into existence. And the truth of this negation and affirmation necessitates the difference between knowledge and power.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This seventh proof focuses on the temporal aspect. When an agent (qadir) brings a possible object into existence, that object now exists. The act of bringing it into existence again is impossible because you cannot bring into existence what already exists (tahsil al-hasil). Therefore, after creation, the object is no longer within the agent's power (qudra). However, the object remains known (ma'lum) even after it exists. Thus, knowledge continues while power ceases, showing that knowledge and power are distinct attributes.

Key Terms
قادر
مقدور
إيجاد
موجد
تحصيل الحاصل
معلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge and power are the same attribute because they both relate to the same object.
Correction: The proof shows that after existence, power ceases while knowledge persists, which is impossible if they were identical. Thus they must be distinct.

Checkpoint
What happens to a possible object after it comes into existence according to the seventh proof?
A) It remains both known and possible.
B) It remains known but is no longer an object of power.
C) It becomes impossible to know.
D) It ceases to be known.

Key Takeaway
The seventh proof shows that knowledge and power must be distinct attributes because after an object exists, it remains known but cannot be an object of power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on your own power to change things or on the knowledge that God knows you completely? Which one gives you more peace when you face a situation you cannot change?
?
If you have sinned and feel powerless to undo it, do you still believe that God knows that sin? How does knowing that His knowledge of you never cease affect your desire to repent?
?
When something you worked hard for finally exists, do you then stop depending on God's power and forget that He still knows it? What would change if you constantly remembered that God knows every detail of that thing even after it is done?
